The Poetical Works of Charles Harpur
Form: poetry
Type: selected work
Author: Harpur,Charles
Editor: Perkins,Elizabeth
First Known Date: 1984
Abstract: 'This collection represents one version of almost every poem written by Charles Harpur, with the omission of some translations and paraphrases. The verse drama, "Stalwart the Bushranger", and the fragments of the dramatic poem "King Saul" are not included. ... The collection is edited from Harpur's manuscript poems held in the Mitchell Library, Sydney, and from printed copies in colonial newspapers when no manuscript version existed.' (Preface)
Publication Details: Sydney: Angus and Robertson, 1984
ISBN: 0207147728
Extent: xliii, 1013p.

Appears In: The Morning Chronicle (ISSN: 1837-3402), vol. 1 no. 67 25 May, 1844 (http://nla.gov.au/nla.news-page4243509) p. 4 (http://nla.gov.au/nla.news-article31742856)
Appears In: The Poetical Works of Charles Harpur, Sydney: Angus and Robertson, 1984 p. 770-771
Appears In: The Turning Wave : Poems and Songs of Irish Australia, Armidale: Kardoorair Press, 2001 p. 26
Abstract: 'Reprinted 25 May, 4, with [a report on] an angry letter from Harpur protesting against editor's changes and the poem in its original form.' (Webby) 
 The first published version of this poem, printed in the Morning Chronicle newspaper on the 11 May 1844, was extensively altered by the Chronicle's editor. 
 Charles Harpur's correct version of the poem is published in the Morning Chronicle 25 May 1844 alongside the editor's altered version of the poem and a column apologising for but defending the editor's alterations. 
 For more information on Harpur's dispute with the editor of the Morning Chronicle see J. Normington-Rawling, Charles Harpur, An Australian (Angus &amp; Robertson, 1962): 98-99.

Keyword: Mutinies &amp; rebellions

Impromptu
Form: poetry
First Line: I like you friend Parkes, but don't like the morality
Author: Harpur,Charles
First Known Date: 1854
Appears In: The People's Advocate and New South Wales Vindicator, 13 May, 1854 p. 8
Appears In: The Poetical Works of Charles Harpur, Sydney: Angus and Robertson, 1984 p. 550
Abstract: J. Normington-Rawling in Charles Harpur, An Australian (1962) describes the circumstances of this poem:
 'In May 1854 Harpur delivered a public rebuke to [Henry] Parkes. The latter won the Sydney [New South Wales] seat in the [New South Wales Legislative] Council vacated by [William Charles] Wentworth when he left for England. At the declaration of the poll, Parkes in his speech of thanks to the electors, uttered two sentences that Harpur had to condemn ... He sat down and wrote some lines and a long note.' (195)
 Harpur's lengthy note is separately indexed.
Keyword: Hubris
Keyword: Opportunism
Keyword: Further reader interpretation recommended
AustLit Ref: http://www.austlit.edu.au/austlit/page/C117147
